All we need from you is a simple cheek swab, a totally confidential medical questionnaire, and your contact information!\n \nGift of Life works to cure blood cancer through cellular therapy. They build a registry of potential donors to increase the chances that someone afflicted with blood cancer will find a good match. When patients under these conditions require donations it's incredibly hard to find a match. That's because stem cell and marrow donations are more complicated than blood. Please RSVP for the workshop using this link. Only those who have RSVP'd will be allowed to participate in the workshop.****\nRhiannon Skye Tafoya is an interdisciplinary indigenous artist from the Eastern Band of Cherokee and the Santa Clara Pueblo Tribes. Influenced by a strong lineage of basket-weavers both paternal and maternal, she continues to use paper-weaving processes to honor her loved ones and ancestors. Her meticulously crafted designs, patterns, prints, and weavings are influenced by basketry and contain themes of cultural teachings, Cherokee language preservation, motherhood and personal and family narratives. Her work is created to archive, preserve and share stories, language, culture, and experiences. Schnitzer and His Family Foundation presents a sweeping survey of over thirty-five objects spanning fifteen years. Catherine Blackburn was born in Patuanak Saskatchewan and is a member of the English River First Nation (Denesųłin&eacute;). She is a multidisciplinary artist and jeweler, whose common themes address Canada's colonial past that are often prompted by personal narratives. Her work grounds itself in the Indigenous feminine and is bound by the ancestral love that stitching suggests. Through stitchwork, she explores Indigenous sovereignty, decolonization, and representation. Her work has been included in renowned national and international exhibitions including Radical Stitch, &Agrave;badakone, Santa Fe Haute Couture Fashion Show, and Toronto Indigenous Fashion Week. She has received numerous awards including the Sobey Art Award longlist (2019/2023), a Forge Residency Fellowship (2022), and an Eiteljorg Fellowship (2021).  \n  \n    \n      From Friday, November 15, 2024 1:30 PM\n      to 2:30 PM EST\n      at Zuckerman Museum of Art.\n    \n  \n", 'Fri, 15 Nov 2024 18:30:00 GMT', 'Fri, 15 Nov 2024 19:30:00 GMT', 'https://owllife.kennesaw.edu/event/10190524'], ['Catherine Blackburn', '\n  Catherine Blackburn\n  Inspired by her late Setsun&eacute;&rsquo;s (grandmother) incredible garment- making, hide-tanning, and adornment, artist Catherine Blackburn&rsquo;s work grounds itself in the Indigenous feminine. Schnitzer and His Family Foundation\n  Jeffrey Gibson: They Teach Love from the Collections of Jordan D. Schnitzer and His Family Foundation presents a sweeping survey of over 35 objects spanning 15 years. The exhibition includes prints, photography, painting, sculpture, installation, and video. Born in Colorado in 1972, Jeffrey Gibson is\nof Cherokee heritage and a member of the Mississippi Band of Choctaw. His vibrant work is a call for Indigenous empowerment as well as queer visibility. Gibson has a Bachelor of Fine Arts from the School of the Art Institute of Chicago and a Master of Fine Arts from\nthe Royal College of Art, London. Gibson is representing the United States at the Venice Biennale 2024&mdash;the first Indigenous artist to have a solo exhibition in the American Pavilion. Historical works on view include a Cherokee Hymn Book, circa 1940; a New Testament of the Holy Bible translated into the Cherokee language, 1860; and a copy of Cherokee Phoenix and Indians&rsquo; Advocate, 1830; among others.
